Franklin County Prosecuting Atty. v. Walker


No. 07AP-165


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2007-Ohio-5095; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 4493



September 27, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by Franklin County Prosecuting Atty. v. Walker, 2008 Ohio 1589, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 869 (Ohio, Apr. 9, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 06CVH-01-321).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a sexually oriented offender (SOO), sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted summary judgment to appellee county prosecuting attorney (PA) in his action, seeking to enjoin the SOO from residing within 1,000 feet of a school premises pursuant to R.C 2950.031.


OVERVIEW: The SOO entered a guilty plea to gross sexual imposition against a child, in violation of R.C. 2907.05, which was a third-degree felony and a sexually oriented offense based on R.C. 2950.01(D). He was convicted, sentenced to community control, and classified as a sexual predator under R.C. 2950.09. The SOO was not registration-exempt under R.C. 2950.04. After the enactment of R.C. 2950.031, the PA filed his injunctive relief action. It was noted that the SOO originally lived in his parents' home, and after being notified that he had to relocate pursuant to § 2950.031, he rented a residence two doors down, which was still within the prohibited range. The trial court granted summary judgment to the PA, finding that § 2950.031 was not unconstitutionally retroactive in violation of Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 as applied to the SOO. On appeal, the court noted that the language of R.C. 2950.031 was meant to be retroactive under R.C. 1.48, and that it expressly applied to the SOO's rental of premises after the effective date of § 2950.031. Further, as § 2950.031 was merely remedial and did not affect a substantive right, it was not unconstitutional as applied to the SOO.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

457 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Mastro v. Glavan


CASE NO. 2010-A-0044


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHTABULA COUNTY


2011-Ohio-3628; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 3067



July 22, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Ashtabula County Court of Common Pleas, Probate Division, Case No. 2010 CV 005.
In re Estate of Hanslik, 2010 Ohio 1490, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 1249 (Ohio Ct. App., Ashtabula County, Apr. 2, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff half-sister (sister) appealed a summary judgment entered by the Ashtabula County Court of Common Pleas, Probate Division, Ohio, for defendants, a decedent's executrix and two beneficiaries, in a suit contesting that will of the decedent.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that R.C. 2107.24 was not retroactive in either its application or effect as it was a remedial, curative law such as was recognized by Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. Section 2107.24 provided the cure of a defect in the decedent's will arising out of its improper execution. As the right of succession was created by legislative enactment, the terms of that succession could be modified by legislative enactment. The application of § 2107.24 did not retroactively divest the sister of any interest in the decedent's estate. The statute was enacted before the decedent died, and before the vesting of any potential interest in his estate. As the admission of the decedent's purported will to probate under § 2107.24 related back to the date of the decedent's death, the sister acquired no interest in the estate upon the decedent's death. The decedent was not intestate until the admission of the purported will. The sister did not have standing to raise an impairment of contracts claim. The application of § 2107.24 to admit the document to probate was a prospective application since the decedent died after the law took effect.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lee


No. 91285


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2009-Ohio-1787; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 1513



April 16, 2009, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CR-333114.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which classified him as a sexual predator pursuant to R.C. 2950.09(C). The inmate had been previously convicted of rape without an age specification, in violation of R.C. 2907.02.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was indicted on three counts each of rape and felonious assault. He entered a guilty plea to one count of rape in exchange for the State's entry of a nolle prosequi as to the other charges. The trial court imposed an indefinite term of imprisonment on the inmate. Four years later, a sex offender classification hearing pursuant to H.B. 180, Gen. Assem. (Ohio) was held, after which the trial court classified the inmate as a sexual predator pursuant to § 2950.09(C). On appeal, the court rejected the inmate's claim that S.B. 5, Gen. Assem. II, § 28 or U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. However, the court found that the evidence was insufficient to support the sexual predator classification where there was only argument by counsel for the State. There were no fact witnesses, expert testimony, or psychological evaluations. Further, the inmate claimed that he successfully completed sex offender treatment programs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court with respect to the inmate's classification as a sexual predator. The matter was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate the sexual predator classification, and to enter a finding that the inmate was a sexually oriented offender. The remainder of the trial court decision was affirmed.

In re S.C.

2005-Ohio-810; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 852

Code Ann. § 2152.17(F) was unconstitutional.

Cosby v. Franklin County Dep't of Job & Family Servs.


No. 07AP-41


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2007-Ohio-6641; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 5818



December 13, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Cosby v. Franklin County Dep't of Job & Family Servs., 2008 Ohio 2028, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 1231 (Ohio, May 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 96CVF-6931).



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant job and family services agency revoked plaintiff home day care provider's certification to operate a type B day-care home because her criminal history made her noncompliant with R.C. 5104.09(A)(1)(b) and Ohio Admin. Code 5101:2-14. An administrative hearing officer affirmed the agency's decision to revoke the certification. The Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) affirmed the revocation. The provider appealed.


OVERVIEW: The day care provider argued that the agency erred by retroactively applying R.C. 5104.09 (2005). The appellate court held that, because the provider had pled guilty to forgery prior the effective amendment date of R.C. 5104.09 (2005), the administrative hearing officer correctly found that the statutory amendment applied retroactively to her, in accordance with the legislature's intent. Although the trial court erroneously found that the challenged amendment operated prospectively only, the error was harmless. The provider was not prejudiced when the agency applied R.C. 5104.09(D) retroactively because its retroactive application was in accordance with the law. The provider acquired no "vested right" to own or operate a type B family day-care home. Further, in light of the overriding purpose of the child care legislation to safeguard the health, safety and welfare of children receiving child care, and the governmental interest in preventing fraud in publicly funded day-care operations, the administrative rule at issue was reasonable in preventing the provider, a past felony offender convicted of forgery, from owning or operating a publicly funded day-care home.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment affirming the order of the agency revoking the day care provider's certification to own or operate a type B family day-care home was affirmed.

Pamela Collins James Davies Estate Mohamed Elwardany v. Geo


CASE NO. 640336, CASE NO. 612104, CASE NO. 633121, CASE NO. 632345, CASE NO. 644696

464 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Toles


Case No. 00CR-02-875


STATE OF OHIO, COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, FRANKLIN COUNTY, CRIMINAL DIVISION


2008 Ohio Misc. LEXIS 316



September 9, 2008, Decided 
September 9, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Toles, 2010 Ohio 2772, 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 2270 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, June 17, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a sex offender registrant, by and through counsel, filed a petition to contest reclassification and application of R.C. 2950.01 et seq. The registrant also filed a motion to stay enforcement of the community notification provision of R.C. 2950.11 until a decision was issued on his petition. The court granted the stay.


OVERVIEW: As a sexually oriented offender under the regulatory scheme in effect when the registrant was sentenced, the registrant was subject to a ten-year duty of registration upon his release from prison and to annual verification of this registration, but he was not subject to community notification. However, under the new registration system of Ohio's Adam Walsh Act, R.C. Chapter 2950, he was a Tier III offender, was to register for the rest of his life, and was subject to community notification. The court found that to the extent that the registration requirements in the Act changed the frequency or duration of the registration requirements, it did not violate Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 regarding retroactive laws. However, to the extent that any provision of the Act changed the form or content of the registration requirements, it did violate Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 regarding retroactive laws. Moreover, the additional registration requirements beyond frequency and duration were clearly punitive in their effect and violated the Ex Post Facto Clause of the U. S. Constitution. Finally, the sex-offender-classification system did not run afoul of the separation-of-powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The petition to contest was granted as to community notification and additional registration requirements beyond frequency and duration but was otherwise denied.

Maxwell v. State


Case No. 2008-CA-202


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, RICHLAND COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3280; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2795



June 30, 2009, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Richland County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 08-CV-264D.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee inmate contested his reclassification as a tier III sex offender, pursuant to R.C. 2950.01 et seq., as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), in the Richland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). The trial court found S.B. 10 unconstitutional facially and as applied to the inmate because it violated prohibitions against retroactive and ex post facto laws. Appellant State sought review.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held it was error for the trial court to find that S.B. 10 violated prohibitions against retroactive and ex post facto laws because such findings were contrary to controlling judicial precedent. Further, it was error to find that S.B. 10 violated the inmate's right to contract, pursuant to Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, because that finding was also contrary to controlling judicial precedent.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

468 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Ball v. State


CASE NO. 2008-L-053


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-4099; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3496



August 14, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Ball v. State, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1508, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 811, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3455 (2009)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000011.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offender pled guilty to gross sexual imposition and attempted gross sexual imposition. He was adjudicated a sexually oriented offender. Subsequently, he was notified of his new classification and registration duties based on Ohio's Adam Walsh Act, R.C. Chapter 2950, as a Tier II offender. He filed a petition to contest the reclassification. The Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the petition. The sex offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sex offender argued that his reclassification as a Tier II sex offender under the Adam Walsh Act was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the sex offender's reclassification was constitutional. There was no abrogation of his prior adjudication because the registration and notification scheme of the new legislation was not punitive in nature, but rather civil and remedial. Thus, there was no violation of the separation of powers. Because it was civil in nature and not punitive in intent or effect, it was also not an ex post facto law or a retroactive law. Further, application of the new sexual offender provisions did not constitute a second punishment prohibited by the double jeopardy provision, in violation of Ohio Const. art. I, § 10. Additionally, the record did not show that the sex offender had suffered an actual injury from any residency restrictions imposed by S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio). Finally, because the registration and notification requirements were merely remedial conditions imposed after release from prison and not additional punishment, they did not affect any plea agreement previously entered into.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

City of Lima v. State


Nos. 2008-0128 and 2008-0418


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


122 Ohio St. 3d 155; 2009-Ohio-2597; 909 N.E.2d 616; 2009 Ohio LEXIS 1600; 29 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 431; 186 L.R.R.M. 2840


January 20, 2009, Submitted 
June 10, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Allen County, No. 1-07-21, 177 Ohio App.3d 744, 2007 Ohio 6419, 896 N.E.2d 149. APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Summit County, No. 23660, 2008 Ohio 38.
City of Lima v. State, 177 Ohio App. 3d 744, 2007 Ohio 6419, 896 N.E.2d 149, 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 5626 (Ohio Ct. App., Allen County, 2007)
State v. City of Akron, 2008 Ohio 38, 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 33 (Ohio Ct. App., Summit County, Jan. 9, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate cases, appellees cities sought declarations that R.C. 9.481 was unconstitutional. In one case, appellants unions sought a declaration that the statute prevailed over a contradictory city ordinance. Each trial court ruled against the cities, but the Court of Appeals for Allen County (Ohio) and the Court of Appeals for Summit County (Ohio) reversed. The unions and appellant, the State of Ohio, sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The cities, in Akron, Ohio, Charter §§ 105a and 106(5b) and Lima, Ohio, Ordinance 201-00, required their employees to live in the respective cities, but R.C. 9.481 barred political subdivisions from imposing such requirements. The trial courts said the statute was a valid exercise of the legislature's authority pursuant to Ohio Const. art. II, § 34, but the courts of appeal disagreed. The supreme court agreed with the trial courts and held the statute was enacted pursuant to § 34 and prevailed over the conflicting local laws, despite the cities' home rule authority in Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3, because no other provision of the Ohio Constitution could "limit or impair" laws enacted pursuant to Ohio Const. art. II, § 34. R.C. 9.481 provided for the comfort and general welfare of employees by allowing them more freedom of choice of residency, so it was validly enacted pursuant to Ohio Const. art. II, § 34. Thus, even if the conflicting local laws were enacted pursuant to the cities' home rule authority, they were still invalid because no provision of the Constitution could "impair or limit" the general assembly's ability to enact laws pursuant to § 34.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the courts of appeal were reversed.

473 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Kelleys Island Caddy Shack, Inc. v. Zaino


No. 2001-1102


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


96 Ohio St. 3d 375; 2002-Ohio-4930; 775 N.E.2d 489; 2002 Ohio LEXIS 2400


June 5, 2002, Submitted  
October 2, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Board of Tax Appeals, No. 2000-B-819.



DISPOSITION: Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vendor paid a resort-area tax and filed a refund request with appellee tax commissioner under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5739.104. The tax commissioner denied the request for a refund, and the vendor appealed to the Ohio Board of Tax Appeals (BTA). The BTA affirmed the tax commissioner. The matter was before the state supreme court upon an appeal as of right.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the vendor argued that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5739.101 violated the Uniformity Clause of the Ohio Constitution, Ohio Const. art. II, § 26. The state supreme court concluded that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5739.101 was of a general nature, as its subject matter was an excise tax. In addition, although there were only three areas in the state that currently qualified for resort-area status under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5739.101(A)(1), there were no limitations or restrictions to prevent other municipal corporations or townships from qualifying in the future. The terms of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5739.101 were uniformly applicable to all qualifying municipal corporations or townships in the state and to all the vendors therein. Because it was possible for any municipality or township throughout the state to become a resort area in the future, given a sufficient change in circumstances, the state supreme court held that the resort-area legislation was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The BTA's decision was affirmed.

State v. Zechar


CASE NO. 09-MA-110


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


2011-Ohio-2630; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 2252



May 26, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Zechar, 2011 Ohio 5605, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 2735 (Ohio, Nov. 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Court of Common Pleas of Mahoning County, Ohio. Case No. 2007CR00649.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Mahoning County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) convicted defendant of two counts of rape, in violation of R.C. 2907.02, and sentenced him to eight years in prison and classified him as a Tier III sexual offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his sentence was contrary to law. The appellate court held that the constitutionality of the consecutive-sentencing provisions were not applicable because defendant was ordered to serve concurrent prison terms. Further, his sentence was not contrary to law, nor did it constitute an abuse of discretion. The eight-year sentences were clearly within the applicable statutory range, pursuant to R.C. 2929.14(A)(1). Also, the trial court considered the necessary statutes in reaching its sentence. The trial court's entry that it had carefully considered R.C. 2929.11 and R.C. 2929.12 was sufficient to establish compliance with its duty. Finally, defendant offered no evidence to rebut the presumption that the jury followed the trial court's instructions not to discuss the case and not to form an opinion over the weekend after receiving all of the evidence. Consequently, it had to be presumed that the jury did in fact follow the trial court's admonition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Barry v. A.E. Steel Erectors, Inc.


No. 90436


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2008-Ohio-3676; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 3105



July 24, 2008, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Barry v. A.E. Steel Erectors, Inc., 120 Ohio St. 3d 1486, 2009 Ohio 278, 900 N.E.2d 197, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 123 (2009)
Reversed by Barry v. A.E. Steel Erectors, Inc., 2010 Ohio 3131, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1661 (Ohio, July 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CV-587362.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employee and his parents, sought review of a judgment from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted summary judgment to appellee employer pursuant to R.C. 2745.01 in appellants' employer intentional tort action, arising from injuries that the employee sustained when he fell while at a construction project. The trial court held that § 2745.01 (effective April 7, 2005) was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employee fell from a construction project. The action alleged that the employee and his co-workers were performing their job duties high in the structure without fall protection equipment. The employer denied liability. The trial court denied the employer's motion to dismiss the action. Thereafter, it held that § 2745.01 was constitutional, as it had been "duly enacted." Further, the trial court found that appellants failed to set forth evidence to show that the employer acted with a deliberate intent to injure the employee, and as such, it was entitled to judgment as a matter of law pursuant to § 2745.01. On appeal of only the constitutionality determination, the court found that § 2745.01 was not constitutional under Ohio Const. art. II, §§ 34 and 35. It represented an invalid exercise of legislative authority because it attempted to legislate employer intentional torts that occurred within the employment relationship. However, such intentional tortious conduct always occurred outside of that relationship. The outcome of § 2745.01 was the same as prior legislation that had been struck down in that it immunized employers from liability for their intentional tortious conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Pat's Bar & Rest. v. Ohio Dep't of Health

Webb v. Progressive Ins. Co.


No. 01AP-534


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2001-Ohio-4056; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 4843



November 1, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrator sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that granted summary judgment to defendants, an insurance company and a driver, in her action for wrongful death.


OVERVIEW: The administrator's decedent was killed while riding in a car operated by the driver. Upon review, the appellate court upheld the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendants. The language in the policy could not be read to conclude that the $ 25,000 limit was available to any claimant separately. Rather, the language at issue clearly consolidated all claims into a single claim. The trial court did not err in so concluding. Former Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.18(H) did not violate the separation of powers doctrine by usurping the judicial authority conferred upon Ohio courts. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.18(H), as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 20 (Ohio), was the uninsured/underinsured automobile liability policy counterpart to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.44. They both purported, in essence, to allow liability policies to consolidate all claims into a single claim. Because it had already been determined that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.44 did not violate Ohio Const. art. I, § 19a, the appellate court felt compelled to follow the ruling in regard to former Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.18(H), at least until the Ohio Supreme Court determined otherwise.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

480 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burchett


Case No. 00CA52


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ATHENS COUNTY


2001-Ohio-2469; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 2298



May 17, 2001, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence in the Athens County Municipal Court (Ohio) for having violated a vehicle overload provision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving a truck overloaded with limestone gravel. Defendant argued the overload statute was unconstitutional because it violated the equal protection provisions of the Ohio and the United States Constitutions. Defendant noted that exceptions to the overload provisions existed for the steel industry, but not the coal and stone industry. Defendant asserted that no rational basis existed for creating two classes of heavy trucks simply because of the industry the trucks serve. Defendant contended that the overload statute violated the equal protection provisions of the Ohio and United States Constitutions because the statute was applied in a discriminatory manner and that no rational basis existed for the discrimination. Defendant failed to meet the burden to establish an equal protection violation. The legislature rationally could have concluded that the distinctions were necessary to preserve the safety and integrity of Ohio's roadways.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence in the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Bower


Case No. 08CA3047


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ROSS COUNTY


2009-Ohio-201; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 160



January 9, 2009, Released


DISPOSITION:  [**1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition with the Ross County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) challenging his reclassification as a Tier III sex offender and the registration and notification requirements resulting from his reclassification. The trial court denied the petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), was an ex post facto law. The appellate court held the Ohio Supreme Court found former R.C. Chapter 2950 did not violate the ex post facto clause in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 because (1) it sought to protect public safety, (2) it imposed no new affirmative disability or restraint, its registration requirements had a remedial purpose, and public access to information on offenders prevailed over any detriment from releasing the information, (3) it did not promote retribution or deterrence as it sought no vengeance and, by itself, was no deterrent, (4) punishment for a failure to register was not applied retroactively for a prior act, but for a violation after the law's enactment, and (5) it was narrowly tailored to the danger sex offenders posed to the public and was not excessive as to that purpose. The general assembly presumably knew of this decision when enacting S.B. 10, and S.B. 10 would not be viewed differently because its changes did not show the prior decision was no longer controlling or that S.B. 10 made Ohio's sexual offender classification system punitive.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State ex rel. Int'l Heat & Frost Insulators & Asbestos Workers Local # 3 v. Court of Common Pleas


No. 85116


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2006-Ohio-274; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 238



January 20, 2006, Date of Journalization



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Writ Denied. Motion Nos. 364124, 363390, 364128, 364117, 364108 and 379351. Order No. 379404.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, unions and individual asbestos litigants, filed an action against respondent court of common pleas, challenging the constitutionality of Am. Sub. H.B. 292, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2004), also known as the Asbestos Litigation Bill (ALB). Relators requested the issuance of writs of mandamus, prohibition, and procedendo with respect to pending or accrued claims. Various motions were pending.


OVERVIEW: Relators claimed that the ALB prevented plaintiffs from prosecuting claims and that it was unconstitutional. They sought issuance of various writs with respect to pending claims and claims that accrued prior to the ALB becoming effective. Intervention was allowed to various parties, and numerous motions were pending. The court did not reach the constitutional issues raised due to procedural determinations, wherein it held that the original actions in mandamus, prohibition, and procedendo were not the appropriate remedy for relators to assert their constitutional claims. The unions lacked standing to prosecute the action, as they were not within the public action standing exception due to the limited scope of the ALB, and they had no personal or private right to secure judicial review. As the actual relief sought was a declaratory judgment and a prohibitory injunction, mandamus was not appropriate. Further, claims were not stated under each of the extraordinary writ claims. There was an adequate remedy at law to all relators by way of a declaratory judgment action, and the litigants also could seek judicial review pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 2505.02(B)(4) and 2505.03(A).


OUTCOME: The court denied relators' motion for summary judgment, granted the dispositive motions of respondent and the intervenors, and sua sponte vacated the entry that granted the motion to intervene of one party.

State v. Hitchcock


CASE NO. 2008-L-032


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-4447; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3773



August 28, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Hitchcock, 122 Ohio St. 3d 1514, 2009 Ohio 4565, 912 N.E.2d 1135, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2499 (2009)
Discretionary appeal allowed by, Review pending at State v. Hitchcock, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1507, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 810, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3378 (2009)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 126 Ohio St. 3d 322, 2010 Ohio 3753, 933 N.E.2d 801, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (2010)
Affirmed by State v. Hitchcock, 2010 Ohio 4980, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 2650 (Ohio, Oct. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 07 MS 000017.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sexual offender pled guilty to attempted gross sexual imposition and was found to be a sexually oriented offender. He was later notified that he had been reclassified as a Tier II sex offender. He petitioned to contest the reclassification. The Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the petition finding that he had been properly reclassified under the new version of R.C. Chapter 2950. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender argued that S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008) was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the Adam Walsh Child Protection and Safety Act (AWA), R.C. Chapter 2950, did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause or the retroactivity clause of Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 because the registration and notification requirements remained civil and nonpunitive in nature after the amendments enacted by S.B. 10. Public safety was the driving force behind the AWA. The AWA also did not violate the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment or double jeopardy. However, application of the AWA to the offender violated the doctrine of separation of powers. The offender's classification as a sexually oriented offender, with definite registration requirements, constituted a final order of the trial court. Therefore, no court could be statutorily directed or required to modify the prior judgment provisions concerning his notification and registration requirements without violating separation of powers and res judicata principles. Final judgments could not be legislatively annulled or modified in situations where the legislature had enacted new legislation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, denying the offender's petition to contest his sexual offender reclassification was reversed. He was required to continue registering as a sexually oriented offender pursuant to the original judgment entry.

 

486 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Vasquez v. State


Case No. 2008-CA-221


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, RICHLAND COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3489; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3010



July 15, 2009, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil appeal from the Richland County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08-CV-0341(D).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Ohio sought review of a judgment from the Richland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which held that S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008), was unconstitutional both facially and as applied to appellee inmate. The inmate was convicted of rape and kidnapping, in violation of R.C. 2907.02 and 2905.01. The matter arose in the inmate's challenge to his sexual offender reclassification pursuant to R.C. 2950.031(E) and 2950.032(E).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of rape and kidnapping with a sexual motivation specification, and he was originally classified as a sexual predator. Thereafter, he was notified that pursuant to the Adam Walsh Act (AWA) and R.C. 2950.01 et seq., as amended by S.B. 10, he was reclassified as a Tier III sex offender. The inmate filed a petition to contest the reclassification, wherein he challenged the classification and the application of the AWA to him. The trial court relied on another case holding in determining that S.B. 10 was unconstitutional because it violated the prohibitions against retroactive and ex post facto laws. Accordingly, judgment was entered in favor of the inmate. On appeal, the matter was stayed pending disposition of the appeal in the precedential case. That case resulted in a reversal of the unconstitutionality holding. Upon lifting of the stay, the court relied on the appellate decision in the precedential case to find that the trial court decision was in error. Rather, S.B. 10 survived constitutional challenge on a number of issues. The right to contract under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 was not implicated, as there was no plea agreement in the inmate's matter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

State v. City of Akron


C. A. No. 23660


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2008-Ohio-38; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 33; 27 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 184; 183 L.R.R.M. 2621



January 9, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Motion denied by State v. Akron, 117 Ohio St. 3d 1496, 2008 Ohio 2028, 885 N.E.2d 954, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 1329 (2008)
Later proceeding at State v. Akron, 119 Ohio St. 3d 1459, 2008 Ohio 4716, 894 N.E.2d 53, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 3209 (2008)
Motion denied by State v. Akron, 119 Ohio St. 3d 1483, 2008 Ohio 5273, 894 N.E.2d 1242, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 2816 (2008)
Motion granted by State v. Akron, 120 Ohio St. 3d 1528, 2009 Ohio 717, 901 N.E.2d 246, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 508 (2009)
Reversed by City of Lima v. State, 2009 Ohio 2597, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 1600 (Ohio, June 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. CV 2006-05-2759.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and the cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city filed a declaratory action against appellees, the State of Ohio and others, challenging the constitutionality of R.C. 9.481. In a separate action, the city's police and firefighter unions sought a declaration that R.C. 9.481 was constitutional. The Summit County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) held that R.C. 9.481 was constitutional and invalidated the city's employee residency requirements. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the trial court erred when it granted summary judgment for the State and the unions. The appellate court held that the trial court erred when it concluded that the Ohio General Assembly's enactment of R.C. 9.481 was within its authority under Ohio Const. art. II, § 34 to pass laws providing for the "general welfare" of employees. Laws passed for the "general welfare" of employees did not encompass a single-issue statute that sought to reinstate a non-fundamental right that the employees voluntarily surrendered when they accepted employment. The sole purpose of was to invalidate employee residency requirements by political subdivisions. That legislation did not address any significant social issues impacting the public at large; it was not part of a comprehensive legislative scheme, but dealt with a single issue; and it applied to a relatively small segment of the population. Finally, R.C. 9.481 was an attempt by the Ohio General Assembly to circumvent the home rule authority of municipalities, under Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3, to maintain residency requirements for their employees.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded.

 

488 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Neal v. A-Best Prods. Co.


Appellate Case No. 22026


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2008-Ohio-6968; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 5799; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P18,150



December 31, 2008, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court). Trial Court Case No. 03-CV-5659.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee executrix sued appellants alleged suppliers of asbestos-containing products in the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) for negligence, negligent misrepresentation, strict liability, breach of warranty, fraudulent concealment and misrepresentation, products liability, and conspiracy, before 2003 Am. Sub. H.B. 292 (H.B. 292) was effective. The trial court held H.B. 292 unconstitutional, as applied, and the suppliers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found H.B. 292 violated Ohio's constitutional ban on retroactive legislation in Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. The appellate court held it was error for the trial court to find H.B. 292's definition of "competent medical authority," codified in R.C. 2307.91(Z), could not be retroactively applied because the Ohio Supreme Court found that it was not substantive, since it was procedural in nature, as it pertained to a witness's competency to testify. It was error to find that H.B. 292's definition of "substantial contributing factor," codified in R.C. 2307.91(FF), could not be retroactively applied because the Ohio Supreme Court held the definition reflected the common-law requirement that asbestos exposure be both a cause in fact and a direct cause of the executrix's decedent's illness and was consistent with the concept of dual causation. It was error to find that the definition of substantial occupational exposure, in R.C. 2307.91(GG), could not be retroactively applied because the Ohio Supreme Court held that it was not a legislative attempt to adopt the Lohrmann test, which the Supreme Court had previously rejected.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings. On remand, the trial court was required to apply H.B. 292 and administratively dismiss the executrix's claim without prejudice.

City of Cleveland v. State


No. 2012-1616


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


138 Ohio St. 3d 232; 2014-Ohio-86; 5 N.E.3d 644; 2014 Ohio LEXIS 40


August 21, 2013, Submitted 
January 21, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from the Court of Appeals for Cuyahoga County, No. 97679,
City of Cleveland v. State, 2012 Ohio 3572, 974 N.E.2d 123, 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 3155 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, 2012).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether R.C. 4921.25, as part of a comprehensive, statewide legislative framework that regulated tow truck operations, was a general law that displaced municipal tow truck ordinances. HOLDINGS: [1]-The Ohio General Assembly could not by statute prohibit the municipal home-rule authority granted by Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3; [2]-R.C. 4921.25, which classified towing entities as for-hire motor carriers subject to Public Utilities Commission of Ohio (PUCO) regulation, was a general law that prevailed over conflicting municipal ordinances; [3]-Because the second sentence of R.C. 4921.25 purporting to limit municipal home-rule authority violated Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3, it was severed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

 

490 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Spangler v. State


CASE NO. 2008-L-062


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3178; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2783



June 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by Spangler v. State, 122 Ohio St. 3d 1469, 2009 Ohio 3548, 909 N.E.2d 1288, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 1934 (2009)
Discretionary appeal allowed by Spangler v. State, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1422, 2009 Ohio 5340, 914 N.E.2d 1063, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2952 (2009)
Affirmed by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000029.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sexual offender contested his reclassification as a tier II sex offender in the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). The trial court denied the petition, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender said R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The appellate court disagreed because it was not punitive. He did not show S.B. 10's retroactive application to him violated Ohio Const. art. II, § 28's bar on retroactive laws because (1) its residency restrictions did not apply retroactively, and (2) its registration and notification provisions were regulatory. It did not offend bars against double jeopardy because it imposed no punishment. He showed no standing to contest its residency restrictions since he did not claim they had an impact on him. It did not violate separation of powers by letting the Attorney General impose punishment because it was remedial, and its registration and notification requirements were collateral consequences of a criminal conviction, nor did its reclassification provisions give the Attorney General appellate review, and classifying sex offenders was a legislative mandate. However, his reclassification violated separation of powers and res judicata principals because his original classification was a final judgment the legislature could not modify.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment reclassifying the offender was reversed, but he was required to continue observing registration requirements previously imposed.

 

491 of 997 DOCUMENTS



City of Solon v. Martin


No. 89586


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2008-Ohio-808; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 690



February 28, 2008, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Criminal Appeal from the Bedford Municipal Court. Case No. 06-TRC-04705.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A city and the Ohio Attorney General, as intervenor, sought review of a judgment from the Bedford Municipal Court (Ohio), which declared R.C. 4506.161 unconstitutional. The matter arose after defendant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol, in violation of Solon, Ohio, Ordinance 434.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was cited for intoxicated driving violations under municipal ordinances. An administrative license suspension was imposed, but defendant was thereafter granted occupational driving privileges for when he drove a non-commercial vehicle pursuant to R.C. 4506.161. Defendant entered a no contest plea to the DUI charge. The trial court granted defendant's motion to declare § 4506.161 unconstitutional as violative of the single subject rule and equal protection. Defendant was restored to full driving privileges. On appeal, the court noted that the issue was repetitive yet capable of evading review, such that it was reviewable. The court held that under the plain language of § 4506.161, it was applicable to suspensions of individual driver's licenses. Further, the trial court had jurisdiction over the matter pursuant to R.C. 4510.13(A)(6) and 4507.16(E). R.C. 4506.161, which was enacted within Am. Sub. H.B. 66, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2005), did not violate the single-subject rule of Ohio Const. art. II, § 15(D), as it had a sufficient common thread with the budget because it preserved federal funding. There was no equal protection violation under the rational basis test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

In re T.W.


CASE NO. 2015-A-0013


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHTABULA COUNTY


2015-Ohio-5213; 2015 Ohio App. LEXIS 5041



December 14, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Ashtabula County Court of Common Pleas, Juvenile Division, Case No.13 JA 115.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A plain reading of R.C. 2152.83(A)(1) and the definition of "secure facility" required a juvenile's classification hearing to be conducted upon his release from a secure facility, defined as having locked entrances and exits, R.C. 2950.01(K); [2]-There was no evidence before the trial court as to whether the facility at Paint Creek had locked entrances and exits and thus, constituted a "secure facility"; [3]-The plain language of R.C. 2152.83(A)(1) and the definition of a "secure facility" were unambiguous, and as such, had to be applied as so; [4]-The differential treatment in R.C. 2152.83(A) was designed to protect the public from the older delinquents as well as to provide the young offenders more opportunity to reform and rehabilitate; [5]-There was no pro se prohibition against Ohio juvenile courts imposing a registration requirement that extended beyond age 21.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

495 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Stetter v. R.J. Corman Derailment Servs., L.L.C.


No. 2008-0972


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


125 Ohio St. 3d 280; 2010-Ohio-1029; 927 N.E.2d 1092; 2010 Ohio LEXIS 723; 30 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 901; 159 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,962


February 18, 2009, Submitted 
March 23, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Stetter v. R J Corman Derailment Servs. Llc, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28611 (N.D. Ohio, Mar. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
ON ORDER from the United States District Court, Northern District of Ohio, Western Division, Certifying Questions of State Law, No. 3:07CV866.
Stetter v. R.J. Corman Derailment Servs., L.L.C., 120 Ohio St. 3d 1450, 2008 Ohio 6813, 898 N.E.2d 966, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 3557 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an injured employee and his wife, filed a complaint alleging that respondent employers committed an employer intentional tort. The United States District Court for the Northern District of Ohio, Western Division, certified questions for review regarding the validity, under the Ohio Constitution, of Ohio's employer intentional-tort statute, R.C. 2745.01, as enacted by Am. H.B. 498, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2005), 150 Ohio Laws, Pt. IV, 5533.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing the certified questions, the Supreme Court of Ohio determined that R.C. 2745.01 did not violate the Ohio Constitution's trial-by-jury provision of Ohio Const. art. I, § 5, the right-to-a-remedy and open-courts provisions of Ohio Const. art. I, § 16, the due-course-of-law provision of Ohio Const. art. I, § 16, the equal protection provision of Ohio Const. art. I, § 2, or the separation-of-powers doctrine, and was therefore constitutional on its face. Further, R.C. 2745.01 did not conflict with the legislative authority granted to the Ohio General Assembly by Ohio Const. art. II, §§ 34 and 35. Finally, R.C. 2745.01 did not eliminate the common-law cause of action for an employer intentional tort.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative and upheld the constitutionality of the statute.

 

496 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


Case No. 03COA016


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHLAND COUNTY


2004-Ohio-2255; 2004 Ohio App. LEXIS 2006



May 3, 2004, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Ashland County Municipal Court, Case NO. 02CRB01799.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Ashland County Municipal Court (Ohio) denied defendant's motion to suppress and to dismiss, he was convicted on a jury verdict of unlawfully possessing two loaded firearms in a motor vehicle (Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2929.16(B)), and unlawfully interfering with a wildlife officer in the performance of his duties (Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1533.67). One of the firearms involved was ordered forfeited to the State. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A wildlife officer entered defendant's property and said he needed to look in defendant's truck to investigate possible gaming violations. Defendant told him he had a rifle in the truck, but his insistence that the officer needed a search warrant to search the truck resulted in his arrest for interference with an officer. The officer found a loaded shotgun and loaded .22 rifle in the truck. The appellate court held that the officer was authorized by Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1531.14 to approach the truck, and when he saw, in plain view, a shotgun with a closed action, its illegality was immediately apparent because Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2923.16(C)(4) required that a weapon carried in a motor vehicle have the action open. Therefore, the officer's warrantless search was proper under the plain view doctrine. Defendant failed to prove the unconstitutionality of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1531.14 on its face or as applied. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2933.41(C)(1) permitted the trial court to order the forfeiture of property used in the commission of an offense; as carrying a loaded .22 rifle was the basis of a charge on which defendant was convicted, the trial court properly ordered its forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

497 of 997 DOCUMENTS


E. Liverpool Educ. Ass'n v. E. Liverpool City Sch. Dist. Bd. of Educ.


CASE NO. 06 CO 61


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, COLUMBIANA COUNTY


177 Ohio App. 3d 87; 2008-Ohio-3327; 893 N.E.2d 916; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 2822



June 30, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas of Columbiana County, Ohio. Case No. 05 CV 48.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union sued appellees school board, financial planning and supervision commission, Ohio Department of Education, Superintendent of Public Instruction, and Ohio State Auditor in the Columbiana County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) to declare R.C. Chapter 3316 unconstitutional, and sought to void the Auditor's declaration of a fiscal emergency. The trial court granted appellees judgment as a matter of law, and the union appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commission, appointed to manage the district's finances when the State Auditor declared a fiscal emergency, laid off union members. The appellate court held the union had no standing to contest the Auditor's finding because, statutorily, only the board of education could. R.C. Chapter 3316 did not unconstitutionally usurp the school board's authority because it was elected, as the Ohio Constitution provided, after which the commission only assumed its fiscal duties in a fiscal emergency. This different treatment of a fiscally troubled district did not offend equal protection because there was no right to an elected school board, so any classification was subject to a rational basis review, and several rational bases existed to treat the district differently. It was no error to grant judgment on the pleadings on a claimed violation of the right to enter into contracts because the statute allowing the commission's appointment was enacted before the members' current contract's execution, so it was not subsequent legislation impairing contract rights. The union had no standing to contest the district's failure to file a statutorily required plan to address the fiscal emergency.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Hale v. State


Case No. 2008CA0113


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, RICHLAND COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3279; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2800



June 30, 2009, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2008CV26D.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate contested his reclassification as a tier III sex offender, pursuant to R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), in the Richland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). The trial court found S.B. 10 unconstitutional facially and as applied to the inmate for violating prohibitions against retroactive and ex post facto laws. Respondent State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held it was error for the trial court to find that S.B. 10 violated prohibitions against retroactive and ex post facto laws because such findings were contrary to controlling judicial precedent which rejected those arguments. Further, it was error to find that S.B. 10 violated the inmate's right to contract, pursuant to Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, because that finding was also contrary to controlling judicial precedent rejecting that argument.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Ohio Democratic Party v. Ohio Elections Comm'n


No. 07AP-876


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2008-Ohio-4256; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 3553



August 21, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Ohio Democratic Party v. Ohio Elections Comm., 2009 Ohio 361, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 269 (Ohio, Feb. 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 06CVF-12-17161).



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an Ohio partisan political party and its chairman, sought review of a judgment from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which affirmed a decision of appellee, the Ohio Elections Commission (OEC). The OEC held that the chairman of the party acted in violation of R.C. 3517.21(B)(1) and 3517.155(D)(1).


OVERVIEW: Campaign materials that depicted the chairman as the sender and that indicated that the party paid for the material were sent to Ohio voters, urging them to vote by mail for party candidates running for statewide offices. Pictures of each candidate with the office they sought to hold were depicted on the material. Based on a complaint by the chairman of the opposing political party, a hearing was held before the OEC. It determined that the chairman violated § 3517.21(B)(1) but that the violation itself was a sufficient penalty. On appeal, the trial court held that § 3517.21(B)(1) was constitutional on its face. It further held that the chairman and the party had knowledge of the implied claim of incumbency represented by the candidate pictures. On further review, the court found no merit to claims that § 3517.21(B)(1) was unconstitutionally overbroad or vague. Further, § 3517.21(B)(1) was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power, and it was not unconstitutionally applied. Clear and convincing evidence supported the finding that the chairman committed a violation of §§ 3517.21(B)(1) and 3517.155(D)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

500 of 997 DOCUMENTS


City of Canton v. Koury


Case No: 2004CA00043


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, STARK COUNTY


2005-Ohio-6189; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 5556



June 20, 2005, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 22, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Stark County Court of Common Pleas, 2003CV00485.
City of Canton v. Koury, 2005 Ohio 3193, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 2975 (Ohio Ct. App., Stark County, June 20, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sign business partners sought review of a judgment from the Stark County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and denied the partners' motion for partial summary judgment in a matter that determined that Canton, Ohio, Codified Ordinance § 110-2202 was valid, constitutional as applied to the partners, and did not amount to a taking that required compensation to the partners.


OVERVIEW: The city council adopted an ordinance which regulated public bench signs. A permit was issued to the partners, allowing them to place bench signs at certain bus stop locations. Thereafter, the city alerted the partners that various signs were not in compliance with the ordinance. In a prior matter, it was determined that revocation of the permit was valid and effective, which decision was affirmed on appeal. The city sought a declaratory judgment regarding the validity of Canton, Ohio, Codified Ordinance § 110-2202, which was an amended ordinance. The trial court found that the ordinance was valid and constitutional as applied to the partners, and that no taking had occurred. On appeal, the court found that the partners had no vested right in the permits. Accordingly, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 713.15 was inapplicable. The bench signs were a nuisance, as they created a safety hazard and impeded sidewalk access. There was no substantive due process violation and there was no taking under Ohio Const. art. I, § 19 and U.S. Const. amend. V. The permits were akin to a license, which was terminable. Res judicata did not bar the litigation, as the prior action involved the former ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

501 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. King


Appellate Case No. 24141


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2011-Ohio-3417; 2011 Ohio App. LEXIS 2892



July 8, 2011, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
(Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court). Trial Court Case No. 09-CR-3539.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from an Ohio Common Pleas Court, which convicted him of improperly handling a firearm in a motor vehicle, in violation of R.C. 2923.16(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's vehicle was stopped for an expired license plate. An officer noticed a metal box, and defendant gave consent to search. After the officer found a loaded magazine in the box, defendant was asked where the gun was located. Defendant indicated that it was behind the driver's seat, and he was arrested. A motion to suppress was denied, defendant was convicted, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the questions posed by a trial court for the purpose of clarifying material facts did not amount to improper examination. Although the trial court erred by finding that U.S. Const. amend. II was inapplicable to laws enacted by the State of Ohio, there was no violation of the right to bear arms. Moreover, R.C. 2923.16(B) did not constitutionally infringe upon a right to bear arms under Ohio Const. art. I, § 4. An equal protection argument under U.S. Const. amend. XIV was rejected because defendant was not similarly situated to a permit holder. Finally, the motion to suppress was properly denied because there was consent given, and the public safety exception allowed the officer to ask about the location of the gun.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

502 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kaiser


CASE NO. CA2005-11-475


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, BUTLER COUNTY


2006-Ohio-7027; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 7040



December 28, 2006 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CRIMINAL APPEAL FROM BUTLER COUNTY COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, Case No. CR2005-02-0274


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Butler County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of participating in a criminal gang, in violation of R.C. § 2923.42(A). The trial court imposed a term of imprisonment on him.


OVERVIEW: Police officers who were investigating alleged teenage criminal gang activity determined that several individuals were members of a particular gang. Defendant was one of those individuals, and the officers observed him and other members of the gang participate in numerous drug transactions. At the time of defendant's arrest, he was wearing a belt with the gang name on the belt buckle, and his cell phone screen displayed the same phrase. A search of defendant's home pursuant to a warrant revealed several notebooks with writings that mentioned the gang name and drug sales. Defendant was found guilty of the charged crime after a jury trial, and he was sentenced. On appeal, the court found that § 2923.42 was not unconstitutionally vague in violation of the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. R.C. § 2923.42, when viewed with the definitions in R.C. § 2923.41, clearly defined for ordinary citizens as well as officials who enforced the law the conduct that was prohibited. Defendant's conviction was not against the manifest weight of the evidence, as there was sufficient evidence that he had knowledge that he was in a gang that was engaging in a pattern of criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Spears


Court of Appeals No. L-99-1338


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LUCAS COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 2229



May 26, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Trial Court No. CR 88-5740.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Lucas County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which found appellant to be a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of rape upon his guilty plea. Thereafter, a hearing was held pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 for sexual offender classification purpose, and appellant filed a motion to withdraw his plea in which he argued that, despite his protestations of innocence, his attorney advised him to plead guilty, that the state withheld exculpatory evidence in order to coerce a guilty plea, and that the sexual offender classification statute was unconstitutional. The trial court denied that motion. On appeal, the court determined that appellant did not show that granting his motion was necessary to avoid a manifest injustice. The court further held that the statute did not violate a convicted sex offender's right to privacy, right to acquire or protect property, or right to a favorable reputation.


OUTCOME: Judgment finding appellant to be a sexual predator was affirmed because none of appellant's constitutional rights were violated.

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

505 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burk


NO. 86162


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


164 Ohio App. 3d 740; 2005-Ohio-6727; 843 N.E.2d 1254; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 6078



December 20, 2005, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Reserved by State v. Burk, 109 Ohio St. 3d 1455, 2006 Ohio 2226, 847 N.E.2d 5, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 1346 (2006)
Affirmed by In re Ohio Domestic-Violence Statute Cases, 114 Ohio St. 3d 430, 2007 Ohio 4552, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2199 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. CR-462150.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Ohio appealed a judgment from the Cuyahoga County Common Pleas Court (Ohio), which dismissed a charge of domestic violence against defendant, in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25, upon a finding that it was unconstitutional in light of Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11 (known as Issue 1).


OVERVIEW: After Ohio Const. art. XV, § 11 went into effect, the trial court analyzed Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25 with respect to a charge of domestic violence against defendant involving an unmarried spouse. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge in part, finding that § 2919.25 was unconstitutional to the extent that it was incompatible with Issue 1. The trial court dismissed the domestic violence charge against defendant and amended the indictment to the lesser included charge of assault. The State appealed as of right. The court found that § 2919.25 was neither incompatible with, nor unconstitutional in light of, Issue 1. There was a reasonable interpretation that allowed both legislative enactments to stand and co-exist. The court concluded that Ohio's domestic violence statute was not a right to be free from family violence that arose from the legal status of marriage, nor was it a crime that was born out of marriage alone. Rather, it involved the theshold factual determination of who was a "family or household member," which determination was not dependent on the legal definition of marriage, but instead, on whether the parties resided together.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

506 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. McClendon


CASE NO. CA2000-02-005


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FAYETTE COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 6099



December 26, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 19, 2001.



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed in part as modified, reversed in part and modification of sentence vacated. This cause remanded to the trial court with instructions to follow the statutory mandates of R.C. 2929.20(H) and (I).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the Fayette County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) decision granting defendant's motion for judicial release, finding Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2929.20(B)(3) was unconstitutional as applied to offenders serving a five year term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery and sentence to five years in prison. He moved for judicial release pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2929.20. The motion was initially denied. After repeated filings and reconsideration motions, the trial court granted the judicial release, finding Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2929.20(B)(3) was unconstitutional as applied to offenders serving a five year term. The court affirmed in part as modified. The court limited its discussion to whether the statute was unconstitutional as applied to defendant. The practical application of the statute as applied to defendant precluded him from filing a motion for judicial release because he would not have served his prison term completely before he would be permitted to file a motion. Likewise, the trial judge had no opportunity to modify the sentence based upon changed circumstances. The purpose of the statute, as applied to defendant, did not withstand equal protection scrutiny under a rational basis analysis. However, the trial court did not follow the mandatory requirements of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2929.20(H), (I).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part as modified because it the statute was unconstitutional as applied to defendant; judgment reversed in part, the modification of the sentence vacated and the cause remanded to the trial court with instructions to follow the statutory mandates in resentencing defendant.

Bumphus v. State


Case No. 2008CA0322


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, RICHLAND COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3345; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2885



June 30, 2009, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2008CV786D.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Ohio appealed a decision from the Richland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which held that S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2008) was unconstitutional both facially and as applied to appellee inmate. The inmate was convicted of rape, in violation of R.C. 2907.02. The matter arose in the inmate's challenge to his sexual offender reclassification pursuant to R.C. 2950.031(E) and 2950.032(E).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two counts of rape, and he was originally classified as a sexual predator. Thereafter, he was notified that pursuant to the Adam Walsh Act (AWA) and R.C. 2950.01 et seq., as amended by S.B. 10, he was reclassified as a Tier III sex offender. Accordingly, judgment was entered in favor of the inmate. On appeal, the matter was stayed pending disposition of the appeal in the precedential case. That case resulted in a reversal of the unconstitutionality holding. Upon lifting of the stay, the court relied on the appellate decision in the precedential case to find that the trial court decision was in error. Rather, S.B. 10 survived constitutional challenge on a number of issues, including the right to contract under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and it remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

508 of 997 DOCUMENTS


City of Bexley v. Conte


No. 07AP-33


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2007-Ohio-5924; 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 5192



November 6, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Conte, 117 Ohio St. 3d 1442, 2008 Ohio 1279, 883 N.E.2d 458, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 761 (Ohio, Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from the Franklin County Municipal Court. (C.P.C. No. 2006ERB07-4651).



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Franklin County Municipal Court (Ohio) with violating Bexley, Ohio, City Code 618.16(e), prohibiting the owner of a vicious or dangerous animal from permitting the animal to run at large. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that, to the extent Bexley, Ohio, City Code 618.16(e) authorized authorities to deem a dog "dangerous and vicious," it was unconstitutional, so it severed "dangerous and vicious" from the statute and dismissed the indictment. The appellate court held this was error because the statute did not involve an unreviewable, unilateral determination that an animal was "vicious or dangerous." Rather, the State had to prove this at trial as an element of the offense, and the dog's owner had a chance to contest that allegation. The statute did not create additional obligations on defendant based upon a unilateral and unreviewable finding of viciousness or dangerousness. Defendant was afforded notice and an opportunity to be heard and could contest the allegation that his dog was vicious or dangerous. Defendant could be found guilty only if the State proved all elements of the offense, including the dangerousness or viciousness element, beyond a reasonable doubt, so all due process protections normally associated with a criminal trial were available to defendant.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

509 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Derolph v. State


No. 99-570


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


89 Ohio St. 3d 1; 2000-Ohio-437; 728 N.E.2d 993; 2000 Ohio LEXIS 994


November 16, 1999, Submitted  
May 11, 2000, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] [EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 1 OF 2. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 20, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County, No. 22043.

In DeRolph v. State (1997), 78 Ohio St. 3d 193, 677 N.E.2d 733 ("DeRolph I"), at the syllabus, this court determined that "Ohio's elementary and secondary public school financing system violates Section 2, Article VI of the Ohio Constitution, which mandates a thorough and efficient system of common schools throughout the state." For the background and procedural history of the events that led up to that opinion, see 78 Ohio St. 3d at 193-195, 677 N.E.2d at 734-735.

In DeRolph I, this court recognized that a new funding system could not be crafted and implemented without time and deliberation. Therefore, we stayed the effect of our decision for twelve months, id. at 213, 677 N.E.2d at 747, in order to give the General Assembly time to enact remedial legislation. We remanded the cause to the trial court, ordering the trial court to "retain jurisdiction until the legislation is enacted and in effect, taking such action as may be necessary to ensure conformity with this opinion." Id.

In entries issued after that decision,  [***2] this court expounded on its order of remand to the trial court. In particular, in response to a request from the defendants for clarification and reconsideration of the decision, this court stated that local property taxes could be part of the revised funding plan, but property taxes could not be the primary means of funding a thorough and efficient system of schools. 78 Ohio St. 3d 419, 678 N.E.2d 886, 887. Furthermore, this court stated that, consistent with the DeRolph I decision, upon remand to the trial court the parties could present evidence regarding the enacted remedy, to establish whether the remedy satisfied the Thorough and Efficient Clause of the Ohio Constitution. 78 Ohio St. 3d at 420-421, 678 N.E.2d at 887-888. The parties could then appeal the trial court's ruling directly to this court, for final determination. Id. at 421, 678 Ohio St. 3d at 888.

From August 24, 1998, through September 3, 1998, the trial court held a hearing on the General Assembly's efforts in the wake of DeRolph I to create a new funding method. Plaintiffs, who continued to assert that Ohio's system of funding public education is unconstitutional, are essentially [***3] the same plaintiffs who pressed that position in DeRolph I. The defendants argued that the revised system complies with the Ohio Constitution.

During the hearing, the trial court propounded inquiries to this court. This court responded by stating that (1) the remand to the trial court involved the Thorough and Efficient Clause of the Ohio Constitution and did not involve the Equal Protection Clause, and (2) the state bore the burden of production and proof on remand, and was required to show by a preponderance of the evidence that the Constitution had been satisfied in order to prevail. 83 Ohio St. 3d 1212, 699 N.E.2d 518, 518-519.

After extensive briefing and the presentation of a great deal of evidence, the trial court issued its decision on February 26, 1999. The decision, reported at (1999), 98 Ohio Misc. 2d 1, 712 N.E.2d 125, is two hundred sixty-three pages in length in the Ohio Official Reports. Upon determining that the state had failed to implement a complete systematic overhaul of Ohio's school-funding system, the trial court concluded that the state had failed to meet its burden of proof that it had complied with the requirements of the Ohio Constitution.  [***4] 98 Ohio Misc. 2d at 263, 712 N.E.2d at 297.

The cause is now before this court pursuant to the defendants' appeal as of right from the trial court decision, under the procedures established in DeRolph I and subsequent orders of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Ohio challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County that the Ohio General Assembly's recent reworking of the laws governing Ohio's public school financing system still left the State with an unconstitutional public school financing scheme.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with the trial court's determination that the Ohio General Assembly (legislature) had failed to show that it had systematically overhauled Ohio's school funding system to pass constitutional muster. Specifically, it found fault with the methods used to measure the equity of district funding, because the legislature had departed from its expert consultant's measuring standards without explanation for its departure. Local property taxes still accounted for the majority of school funding, contrary to court mandate. The measures passed for construction of new facilities and maintenance of existing facilities was inadequate to correct the existing $ 16.5 billion deficit, and made no account for forthcoming maintenance needs. The legislature passed academic standards accountability statutes without passing the necessary appropriations bills to sustain them, in effect worsening the schools' financial positions. Voters did not approve a one-cent sales tax increase passed to increase funding.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed trial court's judgment and extended time for State of Ohio General Assembly (legislature) to enact legislation to bring public school financing system within constitutional compliance, because court was unwilling to completely reject legislature's progress and because process was complex and required balancing of many factors.
