Brooks v. State


C.A. No. 08CA009452


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, LORAIN COUNTY


2009-Ohio-1825; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 1543



April 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by Brooks v. State, 122 Ohio St. 3d 1502, 2009 Ohio 4233, 912 N.E.2d 107, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2348 (2009)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF LORAIN, OHIO. CASE Nos. 07CV154331, 07CV154330, 07CV154329, 07CV154328.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees/cross-appellants sexual offenders contested their reclassifications under Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), in the Lorain County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). The trial court held residency restrictions and provisions denying indigent offenders appointed counsel, in S.B. 10, were unconstitutional but otherwise found S.B. 10 constitutional. Appellant/cross-appellee State sought review, and the offenders cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held the offenders lacked standing to contest R.C. 2950.034's residency restrictions because (1) nothing showed they lived within a proscribed area or had to leave such an area, and (2) they showed no present intent to live in a proscribed area. They lacked standing to contest S.B. 10's failure to give counsel to indigent offenders contesting reclassifications because (1) they sought no appointed counsel, and (2) the same lawyer represented them. S.B. 10's retroactive application did not deny them due process because they were denied no protected liberty or property interest. S.B. 10's retroactive application to them did not offend ex post facto protections because the legislature intended S.B. 10 to be civil and non-punitive, and its effect was not so punitive as to negate that intent. Its registration and community notification provisions did not offend double jeopardy because they were non-punitive. The offenders lacked standing to claim its retroactive application to them impaired contracts, contrary to U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1 and Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, because they did not state who among them entered into allegedly violated plea agreements.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment addressing residency requirements and an offender's right to counsel was vacated. To the extent that judgment found contested statutory provisions constitutional, it was affirmed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

567 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Ohio AFL-CIO v. Ohio Bureau of Workers' Comp.


No. 2001-0642


SUPREME COURT OF OHIO


97 Ohio St. 3d 504; 2002-Ohio-6717; 780 N.E.2d 981; 2002 Ohio LEXIS 3063; 19 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 690; 171 L.R.R.M. 2659


January 30, 2002, Submitted  
December 18, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
As Corrected March 31, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, an Ohio labor union, its president, and a national labor union, filed an original action in mandamus seeking to prevent respondents, the Ohio Bureau of Workers' Compensation and the Industrial Commission of Ohio, from enforcing amendments to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.54 that were enacted in Am. Sub. H.B. 122 (Ohio 2000). A motion by the Bureau and the Commission to dismiss the action was denied and an alternative writ granted.


OVERVIEW: The unions and the union president sought to prevent enforcement of H.B. 122. The issue was whether H.B. 122, which permitted warrantless drug and alcohol testing of injured workers, was constitutional. The court granted the writ, finding that H.B. 122 violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ohio Const. art. I, § 14. The court held that the unions and the president had standing because H.B. 122 implicated a public right. Further, the State's significant promotion of drug testing through the exercise of power created the close nexus between the State and the challenged action required to constitute state action. The collection of blood and urine samples was deemed a search for Fourth Amendment purposes. The warrantless searches, however, could not be justified through the "special needs" analysis because the need for testing did not override the acknowledged privacy interests of individuals. In cases that permitted suspicionless drug testing, the situations and targeted groups were unique and discrete. H.B. 122, however, allowed searches of everyone who worked in Ohio, in contravention of the additional expectation of privacy enjoyed by Ohio workers in the workers' compensation context.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ sought by the unions and the union president.

 

568 of 997 DOCUMENTS


City of Eastlake v. Foster


CASE NO. 2004-L-201


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2005-Ohio-6074; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 5477



November 10, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Criminal Appeal from the Willoughby Municipal Court, Case No. 04 TRC 03984.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Willoughby Municipal Court (Ohio), convicting her of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OMVI), upon a no contest plea, after the denial of her motion to suppress and her constitutional challenge to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(D).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 4511.19(D)(4)(b) was unconstitutional as its enactment violated the separation of powers doctrine. The appellate court held that the trial court found that the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant even if the field sobriety test results were inadmissible. Because the trial court's determination on the issue of probable cause was made independent of the field sobriety test results, defendant's constitutional question was moot. The denial of defendant's motion to suppress was proper. Defendant did not dispute that she was stopped because she was driving her vehicle erratically and exceeding the lawful speed limit. The officer noticed that defendant smelled of alcohol and had bloodshot eyes. Defendant admitted to consuming one glass of wine; however, when the officer asked her for her identification, she presented her credit card. While the results of the field sobriety tests were not admissible as evidence of probable cause to arrest, the officer's observations regarding defendant's impairment sufficed to create the necessary probable cause to arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

569 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Independence Excavating, Inc. v. City of Twinsburg


C.A. No. 20942


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2002-Ohio-4526; 2002 Ohio App. LEXIS 4666



September 4, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. CV 01 06 2638.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant excavation company appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Summit County (Ohio) that granted judgment in favor of appellee city's claim for a declaratory judgment. The company claimed the city's ban on mining and the ordinance providing for the discontinuance of a nonconforming use, Twinsburg, Ohio, Unified Dev. Code § 1139.01(m), were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The excavation company leased a parcel of land within the city that historically had been operated as a surface mine for sand and gravel. The property was zoned for single-family residential use, but was intermittently operated as a mine until 1998 pursuant to a nonconforming use zoning certificate issued by the city, and a surface mine permit. The company filed an application for a conditional use permit to reestablish mining operations on the property. Anticipating that its application would be denied, the company filed a complaint for declaratory judgment. The trial court found in favor of the city. The appellate court found that, based on the stipulated facts, the excavation company contended that the city's prohibition of mining on the property was arbitrary. The appellate court could not conclude on the record that the zoning of the districts containing the property for residential use, and prohibition of mining operations therein, was arbitrary. Further, the appellate court found that the company's claim that the city's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional was barred by res judicata.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

572 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garner


CASE NO. 2008-L-087


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-4448; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3775



August 28, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Garner, 122 Ohio St. 3d 1514, 2009 Ohio 4565, 912 N.E.2d 1135, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2497 (2009)
Discretionary appeal allowed by, Review pending at State v. Garner, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1507, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 810, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3386 (2009)
Affirmed by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000045.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sexual offender pled guilty to rape and was found to be a sexually oriented offender. Pursuant to S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio), he was later notified that he had been reclassified as a Tier III sex offender. He petitioned to contest the reclassification and to be exempted from the notification provisions of R.C. 2950.11. The Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denied the petition and reclassified him. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender argued that S.B. 10 was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that, with respect to the offender, S.B. 10 violated the federal constitutional ban on ex post facto laws because S.B. 10's intent was punitive and its effect was punitive. Those portions of S.B. 10 controlling the sentencing of sex offenders indicated that the classification was part of the sentence imposed and thus, part of the offender's punishment. Further, S.B. 10 was an unconstitutional retroactive law, as applied to the offender. By its terms, it applied retroactively. It attached new burdens and disabilities to a past transaction, since it violated the constitutional protections against ex post facto laws. Additionally, the application of S.B. 10 to the offender violated the prohibition in Ohio Const. art. II, § 28 against laws impairing the obligation of contracts. His plea agreement remained an executory contract at the time of his reclassification under S.B. 10 and, by changing his classification from sexually oriented offender to Tier III offender, the State unilaterally imposed new affirmative duties upon him in relation to the contract. Finally, S.B. 10 violated separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings. The offender was required to fulfill his registration requirements, and all other duties, under his original classification.

 

573 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Curd


CASE NO. 2008-L-048


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3814; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3251



July 31, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Reserved by State v. Curd, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1508, 2009 Ohio 6210, 917 N.E.2d 811, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3415 (2009)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000028.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which reclassified him as a Tier III sex offender as required by the Ohio version of the Adam Walsh Act, Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2009). The inmate was previously convicted of rape, in violation of R.C. 2907.02(A)(2), and he was classified as a sexually oriented offender (SOO).


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a guilty plea to rape and he was classified as a SOO. After the enactment of S.B. 10, the inmate was notified of his reclassification. He contested it under R.C. 2950.031(E) based on assorted alleged constitutional violations. After a hearing, the trial court held that the inmate was properly reclassified. On appeal, the court found that the reclassification did not violate the doctrine of res judicata. As the reclassification was both procedurally and substantively different than the scheme under which the inmate was previously classified, res judicata did not bar the reclassification. Further, the reclassification under S.B. 10 did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers, as the inmate had no reasonable expectation of finality in the collateral consequence of his sex offender classification. The application of S.B. 10 to the inmate was not unconstitutional based on prior holdings. Additionally, the court noted that challenges under ex post facto and retroactivity principles lacked merit, as S.B. 10 was a non-punitive, civil, regulatory scheme. There was no violation of double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amend. V and Ohio Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

574 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graves


Case No. 07CA3004


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ROSS COUNTY


179 Ohio App. 3d 107; 2008-Ohio-5763; 900 N.E.2d 1045; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 4841



November 4, 2008, Date Journalized


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Graves, 2009 Ohio 974, 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 848 (Ohio Ct. App., Ross County, Mar. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
CRIMINAL APPEAL FROM COMMON PLEAS COURT.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to gross sexual imposition, in violation of R.C. 2907.05. The Ross County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to two years in prison and adjudicated him a sexual predator. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it classified him as a sexual predator. The State argued that defendant's challenges to the trial court's sexual predator adjudication had been rendered moot by the passage of the Adam Walsh Child Protection and Safety Act (AWA) in 2007. The appellate court held that the appeal had been rendered moot because the Ohio General Assembly intended for the sexual offender statutes to apply retroactively. Because the AWA applied retroactively, defendant was no longer classified as a sexual predator. Nothing in the AWA amounted to an impermissible or retroactive violation of a vested right. Thus, any error the trial court might have committed in making that adjudication under the old classification scheme had been rendered moot. Therefore, the appeal had to be dismissed because no case or controversy existed to be resolved.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Bd. of Trs. of the Tobacco Use Prevention & Control Found. v. Boyce


No. 09AP-768, No. 09AP-769, No. 09AP-785, No. 09AP-786, No. 09AP-832, No. 09AP-833


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


185 Ohio App. 3d 707; 2009-Ohio-6993; 925 N.E.2d 641; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5858



December 31, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Tobacco Use Prevention & Control Found. v. Boyce, 124 Ohio St. 3d 1507, 2010 Ohio 799, 922 N.E.2d 970, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 658 (2010)
Motion granted by Tobacco Use Prevention & Control Found. v. Boyce, 124 Ohio St. 3d 1537, 2010 Ohio 1557, 924 N.E.2d 841, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 882 (2010)
Affirmed by Bd. of Trs. of the Tobacco Use Prevention & Control Found. v. Boyce, 2010 Ohio 6207, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 3176 (Ohio, Dec. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEALS from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 08CV 005363). (C.P.C. No. 08CV 007691). (C.P.C. No. 08CV 005363). (C.P.C. No. 08CV 007691). (C.P.C. No. 08CV 005363). (C.P.C. No. 08CV 007691).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and matters remanded to trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Ohio Attorney General, the State of Ohio, and the Ohio Department of Health (ODH), appealed from a judgment of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), granting declaratory and injunctive relief to appellee citizens on their claim that H.B. 544, Gen. Assem. (Ohio) was unconstitutional. In addition, cross-appellant nonprofit corporation filed a conditional cross-appeal from the denial of declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Under a Master Settlement Agreement with American tobacco product manufacturers, the State of Ohio received payments from the manufacturers. A tobacco use prevention and control foundation was created in Ohio and was involved in the disbursement of the payments. The foundation's executive director, pursuant to a resolution of the foundation's board, executed a contract with the nonprofit corporation on behalf of the foundation. However, state legislation was enacted which diverted funds to a jobs bill. On appeal, the court found that, because the Ohio General Assembly had plenary legislative power to revoke or transfer public funds, it acted constitutionally through H.B. 544, Gen. Assem. (Ohio) in transferring the monies in an endowment fund to other economic priorities. Thus, Ohio Const. art. II, §§ 1 and 22 were not violated. In addition, the foundation's board violated R.C. 121.22 by improperly convening in executive session and by deliberating upon issues not raised in the motion to convene. The board's resolution resulted from those nonpublic deliberations. Accordingly, the contract between the foundation and the nonprofit corporation was invalid and unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying declaratory and injunctive relief to Legacy was affirmed, but the judgment granting declaratory and injunctive relief to appellees was reversed. The matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Nat'l Lime & Stone Co. v. Blanchard Twp.

577 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Wilcoxson v. Harsman


Appellate Case No. 24095


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


2010-Ohio-4048; 2010 Ohio App. LEXIS 3435



August 26, 2010, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator candidate filed a complaint for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent election officials to certify the candidate as an independent candidate for a judgeship and to place his name on the general election ballot for an election. The candidate further requested an order declaring R.C. 3513.257 unconstitutional for the extra-conditional qualifications imposed on independent political candidates.


OVERVIEW: The elections officials determined that the candidate's nominating petitions lacked the number of valid signatures necessary to place his name on a general election ballot. On appeal, the court, upon review of nominating petitions entered into evidence, found that the officials neither abused their discretion under R.C. 3501.38 nor clearly disregarded applicable law in invalidating signatures on the candidate's nominating petitions. Therefore, the candidate failed to show that he had a legal right to compel the officials to certify his candidacy and place his name on the general election ballot as an independent candidate. In addition, the candidate had standing to challenge R.C. 3501.257 as he ended up with less than the required number of signatures. Finally, R.C. 3513.257 was constitutional as it did not impose a severe burden on voters' and candidates' constitutional rights under the First and Fourteenth Amendment, and R.C. 3513.257 imposed reasonable, nondiscriminatory qualifying conditions on independent candidates consistent with the State of Ohio's interest in regulating the election process. Accordingly, the candidate was not entitled to the requested relief in mandamus.


OUTCOME: The complaint for a writ of mandamus was denied, and the matter was dismissed.

 

578 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smathers


Case No. 05-COA-019


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ASHLAND COUNTY


2006-Ohio-1574; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 1475



March 30, 2006, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Ohio v. Smathers, 2007 Ohio 4445, 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 4009 (Ohio Ct. App., Ashland County, Aug. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from the Ashland County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 04-CRI-090.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Ashland County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) convicting defendant of two counts of burglary in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2911.12(A)(3) and two counts of attempted grand theft in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 2903.02, 2913.02(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to three years on each of the burglary convictions and to 18 months on each of the attempt convictions. One of the burglary convictions was to be served consecutive to the other three terms. The other three terms were to be served concurrently. The high court, under Blakely and the Sixth Amendment, severed Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 2929.14(B), (C), (D)(2), (3), (E)(4), .19(B)(2), .41(A) from the valid portions of the Ohio sentencing statutes. This left trial courts with full discretion to impose a prison term within the basic ranges of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2929.14(A) based upon a jury verdict or admission of a defendant without the mandated judicial findings that Blakely prohibited. Accordingly, all cases pending on direct review at the time of the high court decision had to be remanded for new sentencing hearings in accordance with the high court's opinion. Because the sentence in the instant case was based on unconstitutional statutes, resentencing was required.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The sentence was vacated. The case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing in accord with the law and consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

 

579 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Hayes


No. 04AP-1321


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


2005-Ohio-2961; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 2754



June 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Smith v. Hayes, 106 Ohio St. 3d 1547, 2005 Ohio 5343, 835 N.E.2d 728, 2005 Ohio LEXIS 2358 (Ohio, Oct. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas. (C.P.C. No. 04CVH-05-4975).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sought a declaration in the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that Ohio's Desertion of Child Under 72 Hours Old Act, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2151.3515 et seq., was unconstitutional or that certain of its provisions violated separation of powers, equal protection, and due process. The trial court granted the motion of appellee, Director of the Ohio Department of Job and Family Services, to dismiss. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen claimed the legislation, which allowed the voluntary surrender of a newborn to a "safe haven," denied non-surrendering parents and children their constitutional right to notice of proceedings affecting parental rights. The appellate court held the citizen did not allege he had been injured by the legislation, claiming the public-right doctrine, which allowed a party to challenge legislation even though the party was not directly injured by it, when the issue sought to be litigated was of great importance and interest to the public. The challenged statute was not the type of legislation to which this exception to standing applied, and this was not the rare and extraordinary case that gave rise to the application of that doctrine, so the citizen could not avail himself of this exception to traditional standing requirements.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

580 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Studer v. VFW Post 3767


CASE NO. 2008-T-0133


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


185 Ohio App. 3d 691; 2009-Ohio-7002; 925 N.E.2d 629; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5874



December 31, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
Civil Appeal from the Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2003 CV 2912.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator challenged a decision from the Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee bar in a case arising under the Ohio Dram Shop Act, former R.C. 4301.22.


OVERVIEW: While driving, a patron killed the administrator's daughter. Summary judgment was granted to the bar on the claim under the Act, a negligence case was dismissed, and the trial court found that there was no equal protection violation. This appeal followed. In partially affirming, the appellate court held that a genuine issue of material fact remained on the claim under former R.C. 4399.18(A)(1). The patron was served 9 beers at the bar, and bar employees had multiple opportunities to observe the patron. He was a regular at the bar and admitted to consuming about 8 beers per day. Further, he displayed several signs of intoxication after the accident. Circumstantial evidence could have been used to prove that the bar knowingly sold an intoxicating beverage to a noticeably intoxicated person. Next, liability did not arise under former R.C. 4399.18(A)(2) based on the bar selling an intoxicating beverage to a person who habitually drank beer to excess. This did not give rise to an equal protection violation under former R.C. 4301.22(C). The statutory distinction between beer and intoxicating liquors bore a rational relationship to the achievement of a legitimate governmental purpose.


OUTCOME: The decision to grant summary judgment for the bar on the claim under former R.C. 4399.18(A)(1) was reversed. The trial court's finding that former R.C. 4301.22(C) was constitutional and its entry of summary judgment on the claim under former R.C. 4299.18(A)(2) were affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

582 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nichols


Case No. 99CA532


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, VINTON COUNTY


2000 Ohio App. LEXIS 87



January 11, 2000, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment entered by the Vinton County Court (Ohio), which found him guilty of an overload violation under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5577.04(B) (3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped by a state trooper when the trooper suspected appellant's commercial vehicle of an overweight violation. Based on the totality of the trooper's observations, he believed appellant's truck was overweight and stopped him to weigh the vehicle. Appellant filed motions to dismiss, the court overruled the motion, and appellant was convicted of an overload violation under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5577.04(B)(3), which he appealed. The court held that the trooper possessed reasonable suspicion that appellant was in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5577.04 so that the stop and weighing of appellant's vehicle was constitutional. The court also held that appellant's second assignment of error was meritless as Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 5577.04 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; The trooper possessed reasonable suspicion that appellant had committed an overload violation so that the stop and weighing of appellant's vehicle was constitutional, and that statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

583 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Grendell v. Ohio EPA


C.A. No. 20237


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


146 Ohio App. 3d 1; 764 N.E.2d 1067; 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 4019



September 12, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. 1998 11 4502.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, citizens and coalitions, appealed a judgment by the Court of Common Pleas, County of Summit, Ohio, in favor of appellees, contractor and Ohio Environmental Protection Agency (OEPA), challenging constitutionality of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3704.14 and the validity of a contract between the OEPA and the contractor.


OVERVIEW: The OEPA and the contractor contracted to build and operate a mandatory vehicle inspection and maintenance program pursuant to the statute. Appellants challenged the constitutionality the statute and the validity of the contract. The trial court found for the OEPA and the contractor, and appellants sought review. The appellate court held that the OEPA and the contractor did not jointly own any property and were not joint venturers or partners. Their objectives were different. The statute and the state constitution were not incompatible. Appellants failed to challenge the trial court's findings that the liquidated damages clause presents a question that was not ripe for review, thus foreclosing them from arguing that the clause was unconstitutional on appeal. The appellate court could not consider any error on cross-appeal without a showing of prejudicial error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

584 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Klein v. Leis


APPEAL NOS. C-020012, C-020013, C-020015, C-020021


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, HAMILTON COUNTY


146 Ohio App. 3d 526; 2002-Ohio-1634; 767 N.E.2d 286; 2002 Ohio App. LEXIS 1575



April 10, 2002, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted, Motion granted: Klein v. Leis, 2002 Ohio LEXIS 2017 (Ohio Sept. 4, 2002).
Motion granted by Klein v. Leis, 95 Ohio St. 3d 1433, 766 N.E.2d 999, 2002 Ohio LEXIS 1038 (2002)
Appeal granted by, Motion granted by Klein v. Leis, 96 Ohio St. 3d 1488, 2002 Ohio 4478, 774 N.E.2d 763, 2002 Ohio LEXIS 2017 (2002)
Motion granted by Klein v. Leis, 97 Ohio St. 3d 1480, 2002 Ohio 6866, 780 N.E.2d 285, 2002 Ohio LEXIS 3104 (2002)
Motion granted by Klein v. Leis, 98 Ohio St. 3d 1407, 2003 Ohio 60, 781 N.E.2d 1016, 2003 Ohio LEXIS 185 (2003)
Motion granted by Klein v. Leis, 99 Ohio St. 3d 1520, 2003 Ohio 4161, 792 N.E.2d 1135, 2003 Ohio LEXIS 2111 (2003)
Later proceeding at Klein v. Leis, 99 Ohio St. 3d 1527, 2003 Ohio 4332, 794 N.E.2d 66, 2003 Ohio LEXIS 2141 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Klein v. Leis, 99 Ohio St. 3d 537, 2003 Ohio 4779, 2003 Ohio LEXIS 2418 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Civil Appeal From: Hamilton County Court of Common Pleas. TRIAL NOS. A-0004340, A-0107121.



DISPOSITION: Judgment appealed from affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant law enforcement officers appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Hamilton County (Ohio) which granted plaintiff citizens' claim for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding the constitutionality of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2923.12, 16(B), (C) which banned carrying concealed weapons.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the law enforcement officers and others contended that there were adequate safeguards built into Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2923.12 in the form of affirmative defenses to safeguard the rights of law abiding citizens. The appellate court found that the record reflected that these affirmative defenses were largely ignored at the initial point of contact between a citizen and an officer. The act of carrying a concealed weapon typically resulted in arrest, and affirmative defenses were sorted out later. The practical effect then was to expose a citizen to arrest, indictment, and prosecution for what later could be determined to have been the legal exercise of a fundamental right. Further, the appellate courts found that trial courts applied the law inconsistently, and appellate courts fared no better. The result, which was confusing or opaque to the average citizen--and to police officers, lawyers, judges, and jurors--was an unconstitutional delegation of public policy matters. The appellate found, finally, that when the police, the citizens, and the courts all must guess at the meaning of a criminal statute, subjective and arbitrary enforcement was the result.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified to delete the reference to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 4749.06, .10, and affirmed as modified.

Hungerford v. State


CASE NO. 2008-L-073


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-6997; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 5882



December 31, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Review pending at Hungerford v. State, 124 Ohio St. 3d 1539, 2010 Ohio 1557, 924 N.E.2d 843, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 935 (2010)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Lake County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 08 MS 000061.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant offender filed a petition in the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), to contest his reclassification from a sexually oriented offender to a Tier II Sex Offender as required by Ohio's Adam Walsh Act, Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio), as a violation of his constitutional rights. The court denied the petition, determining that the offender was properly reclassified as a Tier II offender. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before the enactment of Ohio's Adam Walsh Act, Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio), the offender was classified under the former R.C. Chapter 2950 as a sexually oriented offender. He contested his reclassification under the Act as a Tier II Sex Offender. On appeal, the court upheld the reclassification because (1) the Act's regulatory system was not punitive; (2) the Act did not violate the prohibition on ex post facto laws in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10; (3) the reclassification of the offender under the Act, pursuant to R.C. 2950.031, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine; (4) the retroactive application of the Act was valid under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28; (5) the Act did not violate constitutional protections against double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amend. V and Ohio Const. art. I, § 10; (6) the Act did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV; (7) the Act was not a bill of attainder prohibited by U.S. Const. art. I, § 9; (8) the Act was not cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII; and (9) the Act was not a breach of contract and a violation of the right to contract under the Ohio and United States Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pletcher


Case No. 08CA3044


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ROSS COUNTY


2009-Ohio-1819; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 1533



April 16, 2009, Released


DISPOSITION:  [**1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offender contested his reclassification as a tier III sexual offender, pursuant to Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (S.B. 10), in the Ross County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) and moved for relief from community notification. The trial court denied the petition and motion. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender said the application of S.B. 10 to him violated ex post facto and double jeopardy clauses, constituted a bill of attainder, and was not rationally related to a legitimate state interest. The appellate court held S.B. 10 was not an ex post facto law because it was remedial and not punitive. For the same reason, it did not violate double jeopardy, as it imposed no additional punishment. It was not a bill of attainder because it inflicted no punishment. It was rationally related to the non-punitive purpose of protecting the public from released sex offenders because it alerted the public to the potential presence of such offenders, and the legislative choice to categorize offenders based on the crime committed did not make it irrational. It was not error to deny the offender's motion for relief from community notification because, under R.C. 2950.031, it was the offender's burden to show, by clear and convincing evidence, that he was not subject to such notification, but he did not meet this burden, as he presented no evidence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

587 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Whipkey v. Aqua-Chem, Inc.


No. 88240


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3369; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2896



July 9, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Whipkey v. Aqua-Chem, Inc., 2012 Ohio 918, 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 801 (Ohio Ct. App., Cuyahoga County, Mar. 8, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CV-521667.
Whipkey v. Aqua-Chem, Inc., 116 Ohio St. 3d 224, 2007 Ohio 6094, 877 N.E.2d 689, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2886 (2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, a worker and his spouse, sued appellants manufacturers in the trial court for injuries allegedly caused by the worker's asbestos exposure. The trial court held R.C. 2307.93 could not be retroactively applied to the case. The Ohio Supreme Court held this order was final and appealable and remanded the remaining issues to the court of appeals.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturers sought administrative dismissal of the worker's case due to his failure to provide medical evidence of a prima facie case, as required by Am. Sub. H.B. 292, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2004) (H.B. 292). The appellate court held a "savings clause" in R.C. 2307.93(A)(3)(a) allowed the trial court to apply the law that existed before the effective date of H.B. 292 if the court found that a party's substantive right would be impaired by retroactively applying H.B. 292, in violation of Ohio Const. art. II, § 28. However, in this case, the trial court did not deny the manufacturers' motion to dismiss by relying on this savings clause. Thus, based on case law providing that the retroactive application of the procedural requirements of H.B. 292 to a case pending when H.B. 292 became effective did not violate Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, it was error to decline to retroactively apply R.C. 2307.91, R.C. 2307.92, and R.C. 2307.93.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court.

State v. Midcap


C. A. No. 22908


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2006-Ohio-2854; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 2677



June 7, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Midcap, 2006 Ohio 5351, 855 N.E.2d 497, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 2961 (Ohio, Oct. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. CR 2005-05-1634.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictment, which was denied. He then pled no contest to two counts of operating a motor vehicle under the influence of alcohol or drugs (OMVI), under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(A)(1)(a) and (h), with specifications under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2941.1413, and weaving in a lane of travel. The Summit County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) sentenced him to two years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19, as revised by H.B. 163, Gen. Assem. (Ohio), was unconstitutional because it violated the constitutional prohibition against retroactive application of laws and due process. The appellate court held that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19 was not a retroactive law. The penalty enhancement provisions did not punish the past conduct; instead, they merely increased the severity of a penalty imposed for an OMVI violation that occurred after passage of the enhancement legislation. Further, the sentencing provisions, under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2941.1413, clearly reflected the legislature's intent to create a penalty for a person who had been convicted of or pled guilty to five or more equivalent offenses within 20 years of the OMVI offense over and above the penalty imposed for the OMVI conviction itself. Because the legislature had specifically authorized cumulative punishment, it was not a double jeopardy violation. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2914.1413 also did not violate his due process rights as the statute had no effect on defendant's prior OMVI convictions. Rather, it was a mechanism for enhancing his current OMVI conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

589 of 997 DOCUMENTS


City of Dublin v. State


No. 99CVH-08-7007.


STATE OF OHIO, COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, FRANKLIN COUNTY


118 Ohio Misc. 2d 18; 2002-Ohio-2431; 769 N.E.2d 436; 2002 Ohio Misc. LEXIS 5



April 1, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Cities brought action against State seeking declaration that statutes governing use of public ways by public utilities were unconstitutional. On cross-motions for summary judgment, the Court of Common Pleas, Franklin County, Daniel T. Hogan, J., held that: (1) statutes, which were enacted as rider on appropriations bill, were unconstitutional under the single-subject rule; (2) statutes did not violate the uniformity requirement of State Constitution; (3) provisions prohibiting municipalities from relying upon their constitutionally granted powers of local self-government to regulate, and charge a fee for, use of public ways by utility service providers and cable operators, for purposes of installing and operating their equipment and facilities, were unconstitutional under home rule amendment; and (4) question of whether statutes violated the takings clause of the United States Constitution was moot.

Cities' summary judgment motion granted; State's summary judgment motion is denied.



DISPOSITION: Cities' summary judgment motion granted; State's summary judgment motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cities sued defendant State of Ohio, seeking a declaration that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. ch. 4939 was unconstitutional. It was enacted as a rider on a biennial appropriations bill. It limited the extent to which political subdivisions, such as the cities, could control the use of their own public ways by utility service providers and cable operators. Both the cities and the State moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The cities argued, among other things, that the legislation violated the one-subject rule and deprived municipalities of their home rule powers. The State argued that the bill in question was an appropriations bill, which, of necessity, encompassed many items, all bound by a common thread. In rejecting the State's argument, the court found that the rider in question was a non-appropriation rider attached to an appropriation bill. As such, added caution was involved. The court found, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the bill violated the single-subject rule, under Ohio Const. art. II, § 15(D). In addition, the subject was inherently controversial and of significant constitutional importance, as it attempted to deprive municipalities of their powers to regulate the use of their own roadways, in violation of the Home Rule Amendment, Ohio Const. art. XVIII, § 3. Although a municipality did not have the power to effect a termination of a monopolistic utility server in a manner that would be inconsistent with the State's police regulations, it did have the power to enact reasonable, non-discriminatory regulations governing the use of, and fees for the use of, its municipal public ways.


OUTCOME: The cities' summary judgment motion was granted. The State's summary judgment motion was denied. The statutory chapter at issue was declared unconstitutional under the single-subject rule of the Ohio Constitution. It was declared not to violate uniformity requirements. Several sentences were declared unconstitutional, as being in violation of municipality home rule powers, and other statutory provisions were declared to be severable.

City of Akron v. Callaway


C.A. No. 22018


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


162 Ohio App. 3d 781; 2005-Ohio-4095; 835 N.E.2d 736; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 3726



August 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Akron v. Callaway, 108 Ohio St. 3d 1414, 2006 Ohio 179, 841 N.E.2d 319, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 177 (Ohio, Jan. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE MUNICIPAL COURT OF AKRON COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. CR 038138.
City of Akron v. Callaway, 160 Ohio App. 3d 229, 2005 Ohio 1471, 826 N.E.2d 879, 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 1424 (Ohio Ct. App., Summit County, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought reconsideration of the court's prior decision, which was based on defendant's appeal of a trial court judgment, convicting him of obstructing official business and of resisting arrest, in violation of Akron, Ohio, Ordinance §§ 136.11 and 136.13.


OVERVIEW: The city police department received a non-emergency call from a county Adult Protective Services employee, asking them to conduct a "welfare check" on an elderly bedridden male. The police officer who went to the house indicated to defendant, who answered the door, that he was checking for possible abuse, but defendant refused to let him in. XVIII, § 3, and accordingly, defendant's conviction was void. A holding to the contrary with respect to an identical predecessor ordinance was overruled.


OUTCOME: The court granted reconsideration and vacated its prior decision. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Walsh v. Urban


NO. 85466


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


2005-Ohio-3727; 2005 Ohio App. LEXIS 3427; 60 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 833



July 21, 2005, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Case No. CV-490224.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff note holder sought review of the judgment of a common pleas court (Ohio), which granted summary judgment to defendant note maker, dismissing the holder's suit against the maker to collect on a demand promissory note signed by the maker on the ground that the suit was barred by the 10-year statute of limitations set forth in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1303.16(B).


OVERVIEW: The maker made the note payable to her father, and upon the father's death the note was transferred to his trust until the maker's mother died when it was disbursed to the maker and the holder, the daughters of the father and the mother. The maker never made payment on the note, and the first demand for payment on the note was made 12 years after the note was originally signed. In the holder's suit against the maker, the trial court granted summary judgment to the maker on the ground that the claim was barred by § 1303.16(B). On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not err in applying § 1303.16(B), even though the statute did not become effective until four years after the note was signed. According to the court, § 1303.16 was remedial in nature, and the instant case was the very type of action involving a family transaction that the comment to the statute addressed, in which the drafters of the statute stated that § 1303.16(B) was intended to cover a note in which interest due on a note had not been paid because such a case was likely to be a family transaction in which a failure to demand payment could indicate that the holder did not intend to enforce the obligation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Rowles


C.A. No. 24154


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


2008-Ohio-6631; 2008 Ohio App. LEXIS 5524



December 17, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Rowles, 121 Ohio St. 3d 1454, 2009 Ohio 1820, 904 N.E.2d 902, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 1134 (Apr. 22, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Rowles v. Trim, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 145567 (N.D. Ohio, Oct. 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE No. CR 03 05 1336(B).
In re Ohio Crim. Sentencing Statutes Cases, 109 Ohio St. 3d 313, 2006 Ohio 2109, 847 N.E.2d 1174, 2006 Ohio LEXIS 1161 (May 3, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Summit County Court of Common Pleas, Ohio, which resentenced defendant to an identical 30-year sentence after her case was remanded for sentencing consistent with Foster.


OVERVIEW: A combination of concurrent and consecutive sentences had been imposed after defendant pled guilty to 30 separate counts that included kidnapping, felonious assault, and child endangering. The post-Foster sentence was affirmed. The trial court exercised its discretion in selecting specific sentences within defined ranges. As a result, defendant had no right to a jury determination of facts that the trial court deemed relevant. There was no merit to the argument that the Foster remedy of severance of unconstitutional portions of Ohio's sentencing statutes was itself unconstitutional as that was the approach the U.S. Supreme Court took in Booker. Arguments that Foster violated due process and the ex post facto provisions of the state and federal constitutions had been previously rejected. The severance of R.C. 2929.14(E)(4) and R.C. 2929.41(A) removed only the presumptive and judicial findings related to upward departures from a statutory sentence range. The severance did not prohibit the imposition of consecutive sentences. Finally, as there was no ambiguity in the sentencing statutes, the rule of lenity, R.C. 2901.04(A), had no application to defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

Naples v. State


CASE NO. 2008-T-0092


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3938; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 3393



August 7, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by Naples v. State, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1422, 2009 Ohio 5340, 914 N.E.2d 1063, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 2934 (2009)
Discretionary appeal allowed by Naples v. State, 124 Ohio St. 3d 1415, 2009 Ohio 6816, 919 N.E.2d 214, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3634 (2009)
Certification granted by, Review pending at Naples v. State, 124 Ohio St. 3d 1414, 2009 Ohio 6816, 919 N.E.2d 213, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3708 (2009)
Affirmed by In re Sexual Offender Reclassification Cases, 2010 Ohio 3753, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1931 (Ohio, Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2008 CV 831.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate contested his reclassification as a tier III sex offender, pursuant to R.C. Chapter 2950, as amended by Am. Sub. S.B. 10, Gen. Assem. (Ohio 2007) (the AWA), in the Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). The trial court granted the summary judgment motion of appellee State of Ohio. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate said the AWA violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The appellate court disagreed because, under the intent-effects test, (1) the general assembly did not intend it to be punitive, and (2) its effect did not negate that intent, as its registration requirement was de minimis, its requirements were not historically regarded as punitive, it required no finding of scienter, it did not promote retribution or deterrence, the behavior it applied to was not already a crime, it had an alternate purpose of public protection, and it was not excessive given that purpose. It was not unconstitutionally retroactive, under Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, because (1) it was intended to be retroactive, and (2) it was remedial. His reclassification did not violate his right to contract, due to his plea bargain, because that contract was completed when he pled guilty and was sentenced. His reclassification violated separation of powers and res judicata doctrines because (1) his former classification was a final order, so no court could be statutorily ordered to modify it, and (2) it imposed enhanced requirements, changing the prior judgment in which he had a reasonable expectation of finality.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, but the inmate was required to continue registering as a sexual predator.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to four counts of aggravated robbery. He was sentenced to 16 years in prison. He later filed a motion to vacate sentence. State v. Irvin


Case No. 08CA3057


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ROSS COUNTY


2009-Ohio-3128; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 2671



June 23, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Review pending at State v. Irvin, 123 Ohio St. 3d 1492, 2009 Ohio 6015, 916 N.E.2d 1073, 2009 Ohio LEXIS 3242 (2009)
Review pending at State v. Irvin, 126 Ohio St. 3d 1534, 2010 Ohio 3825, 931 N.E.2d 1097, 2010 Ohio LEXIS 1956 (2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by Cases Held for the Decision in State v. Williams, 130 Ohio St. 3d 254, 2011 Ohio 5348, 957 N.E.2d 289, 2011 Ohio LEXIS 2649 (2011)
Motion denied by State v. Irvin, 2012 Ohio 2025, 2012 Ohio LEXIS 1025 (Ohio, May 9, 2012)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Ross County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) convicted defendant of three counts of unlawful sexual conduct with a minor, one count of gross sexual imposition, and two counts of rape, under former R.C. 2907.02(A)(1)(b). He was designated as a Tier III sex offender and sentenced to 20 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in sentencing him to mandatory five-year prison terms for each of his rape convictions. The appellate court held that the five-year sentences for each of defendant's rape convictions were neither clearly and convincingly contrary to law nor an abuse of discretion. His rape convictions resulted from the calculated and repeated victimization of two young boys who were under his supervision and who looked upon him as a trusted family friend. Defendant did not demonstrate that the combined 10 years that he received for the two rape convictions was unwarranted. Because rape was a first-degree felony, defendant was subject to a mandatory term of three to 10 years for each conviction pursuant to R.C. 2929.13(F)(2). Further, there was no due process violation because defendant was given notice and an opportunity to be heard at his sexual offender classification hearing. As a convicted sex offender, he had no settled expectations or vested rights as to the registration obligations imposed upon him. Finally, because the provisions of R.C. Chapter 2950 were remedial in nature, not punitive, there was no violation of ex post facto or double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

McKinley v. Ohio Bureau of Workers' Comp.


Case No. 06CA7


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, WASHINGTON COUNTY


170 Ohio App. 3d 161; 2006-Ohio-5271; 866 N.E.2d 527; 2006 Ohio App. LEXIS 5254



September 26, 2006, Released  
September 26, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by McKinley v. Ohio Bureau of Workers' Comp., 112 Ohio St. 3d 1489, 2007 Ohio 724, 862 N.E.2d 116, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 394 (2007)
Motion denied by McKinley v. Ohio Bureau of Workers' Comp., 116 Ohio St. 3d 1408, 2007 Ohio 6140, 876 N.E.2d 967, 2007 Ohio LEXIS 2899 (2007)
Affirmed by McKinley v. Ohio Bureau of Workers' Comp., 117 Ohio St. 3d 538, 2008 Ohio 1736, 885 N.E.2d 242, 2008 Ohio LEXIS 998 (Ohio, Apr. 16, 2008)



DISPOSITION:  JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee workers' compensation claimant brought an action in the Washington County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) challenging the constitutionality of R.C. §§ 4123.93 and 4123.931, after appellant, the Ohio Bureau of Workers' Compensation, asserted a subrogation right against the claimant's tort settlement. The trial court found the statutes violated Ohio Const. art. I, §§ 2, 16 and 19, and the Bureau appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant said R.C. §§ 4123.93 and 4123.931 denied him due process by assuming his tort settlement was a double recovery for benefits the Bureau paid and providing no way to litigate the subrogation amount. The appellate court held the statutes' current versions were not unconstitutional, under Ohio Const. art. I, §§ 2, 16 and 19 because the claimant did not have to reimburse the Bureau for benefits not received, could keep any remainder of his tort award after the Bureau's duty to make payments ended, guarding against its windfall and doing away with his risk of overestimating liability for future values, and the potential for a disparate result between the claimant, who settled his tort claim, and those who tried their claims was eliminated. The state had a legitimate interest in minimizing losses to the workers' compensation fund and self-insuring employers due to third-party tortfeasors to the extent it barred the claimant's double recovery, and, as the Bureau only recouped to the extent there was a double recovery, and the claimant had a substantial opportunity to show amounts that were not a double recovery, equal protection was not violated.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

 

600 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Henson v. Cleveland Steel Container Corp


CASE NO. 2008-P-0053


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, PORTAGE COUNTY


2009-Ohio-180; 2009 Ohio App. LEXIS 177; 28 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1199



January 16, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 2006-CV-1227.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former employee appealed the summary judgment (Civ. R. 56(C)) entered in favor of appellee, her former employer, by the Portage County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio). At issue was whether a genuine issue of material fact existed on the former employee's intentional tort claim.


OVERVIEW: Three of the former employee's fingers had been partially severed by a punch press machine. The former employee argued that the current version of R.C. 2745.01(A), which governed causes of action premised upon employer intentional torts, was unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment to the former employer on the basis of this statute. The appeals court agreed. Since R.C. 2745.01(A) had been found unconstitutional, the court followed the Fyffe test in analyzing the former employee's claim. In order to avoid summary judgment, she was required to produce Civ. R. 56 evidentiary materials demonstrating that the former employer knew she was placing fittings directly in a die without using wrist restraints, as she was required to do by the former employer's policy. This she failed to do. She conceded that she was trained by the former employer's manufacturing manager that whenever a press operator used a press, he or she was required to use wrist restraints. Because there was no evidence in the record that the former employer had knowledge of the existence of a dangerous condition in its workplace, the former employee's argument lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.
